Answering the Objection of Non-Persisting Accidents
The author gives two responses to the objection about non-persisting accidents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two responses to the objection that some accidents cannot persist.

Core Idea
Accidents can persist either inherently or due to an accidental quality.

The author now addresses the first objection raised against the possibility of accidents persisting. He presents two distinct responses: one affirming that all accidents can persist, and another that explains the impossibility as stemming from an accidental quality. Both responses aim to defend the rational possibility of accident persistence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: 'The answer to the first objection' followed by two sections.
The passage is a direct response to a specific objection.
2
Identify the two responses
The passage contains two distinct answers. Find the transition phrase 'وأما الذين سلموا' which introduces the second response.
The first response is for those who say all accidents can persist; the second is for those who accept some cannot.
3
Understand the first response
The first response argues that every accident can persist because its essence is receptive to existence, and that receptivity is a necessary concomitant of the essence, so it remains forever.
This view makes the objection vanish entirely.
4
Understand the second response
For those who concede some accidents cannot persist, the answer is that persistence itself is an accidental quality (kayfiyya). What is impossible is the occurrence of that quality, which is not receptive to existence.
This explains the impossibility without denying the accident's own potential.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما أقمنا البرهان القاطع على فساد الاحتمال الذي ذكرتموه ، فلنذكر الجواب على الوجوه التي عولوا عليها : الجواب عن الشبهة الأولى : وهي قولهم : ( إن من الأعراض ما يكون ممتنع البقاء ) . فنقول : من الناس من قال كل عرض فإنه يجوز بقاؤه ، قال : لان تلك الماهية قابلة للوجود ، وإنها لو لم تكن قابلة للوجود لما وجدت تلك القابلية من لوازم الماهية ، ولازم الماهية يكون واجب الدوام بدوام الماهية ، فتلك القابلية باقية أبدا ، فكان ذلك الشيء ممكن البقاء والدوام، وعلى هذا المذهب فالإشكال زائل وأما الذين سلموا : أن من الأعراض ما يمتنع بقاؤه . فنقول : جواب هذه الشبهة عندهم : أن كونه باقيا كيفية حادثة ، فالممتنع هو حصول تلك الكيفية ، وهي غير قابلة للوجود أصلا .
And since we have presented the decisive proof of the invalidity of the possibility that you mentioned, we will now present the answer to the aspects on which they relied: The answer to the first objection: which is their saying: 'Among accidents there are those that cannot persist.' We say: Among people are those who say that every accident is permissible to persist. He said: Because that essence is receptive to existence, and if it were not receptive to existence, that receptivity would not exist from the concomitants of the essence. And the concomitant of the essence is necessarily perpetual with the perpetuity of the essence. So that receptivity remains forever, so that thing is possible of persistence and perpetuity. On this doctrine, the difficulty vanishes. As for those who concede that among accidents there are those the persisting of which is impossible, we say: The answer to this objection according to them is that its being persistent is an accidental quality (kayfiyya haditha). What is impossible is the occurrence of that quality, and it is not receptive to existence at all.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is the answer to the first objection. The author presents two responses to the claim that some accidents cannot persist. The first response is that all accidents can persist because their essence is receptive to existence, and that receptivity is a necessary concomitant of the essence, so it remains forever. On this view, the objection disappears. The second response, for those who accept that some accidents cannot persist, is that the attribute of persistence is an accidental quality (kayfiyya haditha). What is impossible is the occurrence of that quality itself, which is not receptive to existence at all. So the accident's non-persistence is due to the impossibility of the quality, not to any inherent limitation of the accident itself.

Key Terms
عرض
بقاء
كيفية حادثة
لازم الماهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The two responses contradict each other.
Correction: They are alternative positions held by different scholars, not contradictory. Both are valid ways to answer the objection.

Checkpoint
According to the second response to the first objection, why is the impossibility of persistence of some accidents explained?
A) Because accidents are inherently transient.
B) Because the quality of persistence is a non-receptive accidental quality.
C) Because the essence is not receptive to existence.
D) Because the cause is missing.

Key Takeaway
The objection that some accidents cannot persist is answered either by affirming all accidents can persist or by attributing non-persistence to an accidental quality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter objections to your beliefs, do you seek out multiple valid responses as this lesson does, or do you immediately dismiss the objection? What does your default reaction reveal about your trust in the strength of your faith?
?
The author presents two different positions that both resolve the difficulty. Are you able to accept that multiple theological viewpoints can be valid, or do you feel the need for a single 'right' answer? How might this affect your interactions with others who differ?
?
Everything that exists persists only by Allah's continuous will. Do you live with the constant awareness that your own existence is a gift renewed every moment, or do you take it for granted? Write one tangible action you can take today to acknowledge your complete dependence on Allah for your continued existence.

Distinction Between Essence and Existence as a Proof for Possibility
Beginning of the second philosophers' proof for the possibility of bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophical argument that separates essence from existence to establish the possibility of bodies.

Core Idea
If existence is separate from essence, the thing is possible, not necessary.

The philosophers present a concise argument for the contingency of bodies. They claim that for any body, its existence is not the same as its essence, and anything with such a separation is inherently possible. This short passage sets the stage for deeper discussions about necessity and contingency.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the proof is stated in two short statements.
2
Identify the two premises
The passage contains a minor premise and a major premise. Find the statement about bodies and the conditional statement about anything whose existence is other than its essence.
3
Understand the key terms
Focus on the terms 'essence' (الماهية) and 'existence' (الوجود). In this context, essence is what something is, existence is that it is. The distinction is crucial.
In necessary beings, essence and existence are identical.
4
Derive the conclusion
Combine the two premises: All bodies have existence distinct from essence. Whatever has that distinction is possible. Therefore, all bodies are possible. Write this conclusion in your own words.
The conclusion is implied but not explicitly restated.
5
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself why proving bodies are possible matters. It leads to the need for a cause (the Necessary Being) and establishes contingency, a key concept in Islamic theology.
This proof is one of several used by philosophers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية للفلاسفة في إثبات كون الأجسام ممكنة الوجود لذواتها: قالوا: كل جسم فإن وجوده غير ماهيته وكل ما وجوده غير ماهيته، فهو ممكن
The second proof of the philosophers for establishing that bodies are possible in existence in themselves: They said: Every body, its existence is other than its essence, and everything whose existence is other than its essence is possible.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage introduces the second proof for the possibility of bodies. The proof is stated concisely: for every body, its existence is distinct from its essence (i.e., existence is not part of the definition of body). And anything whose existence is not identical to its essence is possible (mumkin) rather than necessary (wajib). This is a foundational principle in Islamic philosophy and kalam: necessary existence belongs only to God, whose essence is identical with existence; contingent things have existence added to their essence. The proof is only begun here; further elaboration would follow in subsequent text. The passage serves as a clear statement of the premise that will be used to argue for the contingency of bodies.

Key Terms
الماهية
الوجود
الممكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that 'existence is other than essence' itself defines possibility, without needing further argument to establish that bodies indeed have distinct essences and existences.
Correction: The passage states the distinction as a premise for possibility; it does not argue for the distinction itself. The proof requires that the distinction be accepted or proven elsewhere.

Checkpoint
According to this proof, what follows if a body's existence is distinct from its essence?
A) The body is necessary.
B) The body is possible.
C) The body is eternal.
D) The body is composed.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers argue that the distinction between essence and existence in bodies proves their possibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your existence is entirely separate from your essence—meaning you could have not existed—how does that change your sense of self-importance? Are you living as if you are the source of your own being?
?
The proof shows that your body, and everything about you, is contingent and dependent on a cause. Have you truly felt that dependence in your daily life? What would change if you woke up every morning remembering that you are not self-sufficient?
?
If the distinction between essence and existence proves that you are possible and need a Necessary Being, what does that demand from you right now, in this moment, regarding your relationship with Allah?
